<title>IG</title> 2.1b, etc., and prevails in Ptolemaic papyri; Inscrr. vary,

Supp. 761.] (βύβλος, βύβλινος, βυβλίον, etc., are the original forms: βιβλ- seems to have arisen in Attic by assimilation in βιβλίον, and is found in earlier Attic Inscrr., cf. ἐπί
in column (v. κέρας V 3c): metaph., 
<i>in</i> column (v. κέρας V 3c): metaph., 
 of the quarter or direction towards or in which a thing takes place, ἐ. δεξιά, ἐπʼ ἀριστερά, to the right or left, Il. 7.238, 12.240, Od. 3.171, Hdt. 6.33, etc.; ἐ. τὰ ἕτερα or ἐ. θάτερα, Id. 5.74, Th. 1.87, etc.; ἐ. τὰ μακρότερα ,βραχύτερα, on the longer, shorter side, Hdt. 1.50; ἐπʼ ἀμφότερα νοέων both ways, Id. 8.22; ἐπʼ ἀμφότερα μαχᾶν τάμνειν τέλος Pi. O. 13.57, etc.; ἐ. τάδε Φασήλιδος on this side, Isoc. 7.80; ἐ. ἐκεῖνα, v. ἐπέκεινα; ἐφʼ ἕν, ἐ. δύο, ἐ. τρία, of space, in one, two, three dimensions, Arist. de An. 404b23, Plot. 6.3.13; in Military phrases, ἐ. δόρυ ἀναστρέψαι ,ἐ. ἀσπίδα μεταβαλέσθαι, to the spear or shield side, i.e. to  right or left, X. An. 4.3.29, Cyr. 7.5.6; ἐ. πόδα ἀναχωρεῖν, etc., retire on the foot, i.e. facing the enemy, Id. An. 5.2.32; so ἐ. κέρας or ἐ. κέρως πλεῖν, etc., sail towards or on the wing, i.e. in column (v. κέρας V 3c): metaph., ἐ. τὸ μεῖζον κοσμῆσαι, δεινῶσαι, etc., with exaggeration, Th. 1.10, 8.74, etc.; ἐ. τὸ πλέον ἀγγέλλεσθαι Id. 6.34; ἐ. τὸ φοβερώτερον ib. 83; ἐ. τὰ γελοιότερα ἐπαινέσαι so as to provoke laughter, Pl. Smp. 214e; ἐ. τὰ καλλίω, ἐ. τὰ αἰσχίονα, Id. Plt. 293e; ἐ. τὸ βέλτιον καὶ κάλλιον, ἐ. τὸ χεῖρον καὶ τὸ αἴσχιον, Id. R. 381b; ἐ. τὸ ἄμεινον Orac. ap. D. 43.66.

ἐρείπιον
CIG 2700e (
<title>CIG</title> 2700e (
fallen ruin, wreck, Arist. Rh. 1413a6, Aristid. Or. 49(25).42, Opp. H. 5.324: generally in pl., ναυτικὰ ἐ. wreckage, A. Ag. 660, Fr. 274, E. Hel. 1080 ; θραύμασίν τʼ ἐρειπίων A. οὐ
μή, v. μή B. 5c; sts. we have 
<foreign lang="greek">μή</foreign>, v. μή B. 5c; sts. we have 
 οὐ is used with inf. in orat. obliq., when it represents the ind. of orat. recta, φαμὲν δέ οἱ οὐ τελέεσθαι Od. 4.664, cf. Il. 17.174, 21.316, S. Ph. 1389, etc.; λέγοντες οὐκ εἶναι αὐτόνομοι Th. 1.67, cf. Pl. R. 348c, X. Cyr. 1.6.18; οἶμαι . . οὐκ ὀλίγον ἔργον αὐτὸ εἶναι Pl. R. 369b, cf. S. OT 1051, Th. 1.71, etc.; ἡγήσαντο ἡμᾶς οὐ περιόψεσθαι ib. 39. (For the occasional use of μή, v. μή B. 5c; sts. we have οὐ and μή in consecutive clauses, οἶμαι σοῦ κάκιον οὐδὲν ἂν τούτων κρατύνειν μηδʼ ἐπιθύνειν χερί S. Ph. 1058 sq.; αὐτὸ ἡγοῦμαι οὐ διδακτὸν εἶναι μηδὲ . . παρασκευαστόν Pl. Prt. 319b.)

οὐδός
GDI 5601a (
<title>GDI</title> 5601a (
 metaph., ἐπὶ γήραος οὐδῷ on the threshold which is old age, i.e. perh., on the threshold that leads from life to death (so οὐδὸς βιότου the end of life, Q.S. 10.426), Il. 22.60, Od. 15.348, Hes. Op. 331, Hdt. 3.14, cf. Pl. R. 328e; ἐπὶ γήρως ὀδῷ Lycurg., Hyp., and Men. ll. cc.; μέχρι γήραος οὐδοῦ Ps.-Phoc. 230; γήραος οὐδὸν ἱκέσθαι Od. 23.212, cf. 15.246.—Poet. word, used by Arist. Metaph. 1042b19, Plu. TG 17, and Luc. Dom. 18, al., in the form οὐδός, which is Ion., cf. Hp. Art. 78, GDI 5601a (Ephesus), IG ΙΙ(2).158 A 69 (Delos, iii B. C.), and is used later as gloss on  βηλός, AB 224 (so ὀδός in 225 and Hsch. s.v. ὀρρόβηλος). (The forms οὐδός ὠδός ὀδός point to *ὀδϝός.)

rhombus-shaped, rhomboidal, Hp. Art. 35, Str. 2.1.22, etc.; ῥ. σχῆμα rhomboid, i.e. a four-sided figure with only the opposite sides and angles equal, Euc. 1 Def. 22, Ph. Bel. 52.30, Ptol. Alm. 7.5, cf. Hegesand. 37; τὸ ῥ. στερεόν (v. ῥόμβος B. 1b) Simp. in Cael. 410.5:—τὸ ῥ., a place at Megara, Plu. Thes. 27.

τακτικός
Fr. 28b). 
<title>Fr.</title> 28b). 
fit for ordering, or arranging, esp. in war, τ. ἀνήρ tactician, X. τέττιξ
Phdr. 262d; but they also became a prov. for garrulity, 
<title>Phdr.</title> 262d; but they also became a prov. for garrulity, 
cicala, Cicada plebeia or allied species, a winged insect fond of basking on trees, when the male makes a chirping or clicking noise by means of certain drums or ‘tymbals’ underneath the wings, whence the joke in Xenarch. 14, εἶτʼ . . οἱ τέττιγες οὐκ εὐδαίμονες, ὧν ταῖς γυναιξὶν οὐδʼ ὁτιοῦν φωνῆς ἔνι; prov., τέττιγος ἐδράξω πτεροῦ Archil. 143 (v. συλλαμβάνω II.1). This noise is freq. used as a simile for sweet sounds, Il. 3.151, Hes. Op. 582, Sc. 393, Simon. 173, 174, etc.; and Plato calls them οἱ Μουσῶν προφῆται, Phdr. 262d; but they also became a prov. for garrulity, λαλεῖν τέττιξ Aristopho 10.7: τ. πολλοὶ γινόμενοι νοσῶδες τὸ ἔτος σημαίνουσι Thphr. Sign. 54. They were thought to sing continually without food or drink, Ar. Nu. 1360, Pl. Phdr. 259c; or on a diet of air and dew, Arist. HA 532b13, Theoc. 4.16, AP 6.120 (Leon.), Anacreont. 32, Plu. 2.660f. The Greeks ate τέττιγες to whet the appetite, Ath. 4.133b, cf. Ar. Frr. 51, 569.4, Alex. 162.13 (anap.), Anaxandr. 41.59 (anap., unless here the τέττιξ ἐνάλιος is meant, v. infr. II); and as a medical remedy, Dsc. 2.51, Orib. Fr. 64. 
<sense id="n103637.0" n="" level="1" opt="n"><i>cicala, Cicada plebeia</i> or allied species, a winged insect fond of basking on trees, when the male makes a chirping or clicking noise by means of certain drums or ‘tymbals’ underneath the wings, whence the joke in <bibl n="Perseus:abo:tlg,0518,001:14" default="NO"><author>Xenarch.</author> 14</bibl>, <foreign lang="greek">εἶτʼ . . οἱ τέττιγες οὐκ εὐδαίμονες, ὧν ταῖς γυναιξὶν οὐδʼ ὁτιοῦν φωνῆς ἔνι</foreign>; prov., <cit><quote lang="greek">τέττιγος ἐδράξω πτεροῦ</quote> <bibl n="Perseus:abo:tlg,0232,001:143" default="NO"><author>Archil.</author> 143</bibl></cit> (v. συλλαμβάνω II.1). ὕπειμι
ὑπῄει μοι τὸ γιγνόμενον Plu. 2 652b. 
<cit><quote lang="greek">ὑπῄει μοι τὸ γιγνόμενον</quote> <author>Plu.</author> 2</cit> 652b.

(Pap.); this contradiction in the early evidence is unexplained; the form <foreign lang="greek">φιδ-</foreign> or <foreign lang="greek">φειδ-</foreign> is corroborated by <bibl n="Perseus:abo:tlg,0007,004:12" default="NO"><author>Plu.</author> <title>Lyc.</title> 12</bibl>, where it is suggested that the word comes from <foreign lang="greek">φιλία</foreign> with substitution of <itype lang="greek" opt="n">δ</itype> for <itype lang="greek" opt="n">λ</itype>, or from <foreign lang="greek">φειδώ,</foreign> or from <foreign lang="greek">*ἐδίτια</foreign> (‘eatings’, cf. <foreign lang="greek">ἐδωδή</foreign>) with prefixed <foreign lang="greek">φ.</foreign> Codd. have <foreign lang="greek">φιδίτια</foreign> (or <itype lang="greek" opt="n">ον</itype>) in <author>Arist.</author> <title>Pol.</title> (v.l. φιλίτια), <author>Plu.</author> (exc. <foreign lang="greek">φιτιδίοις</foreign> <abbr>v.</abbr> l. in <title>Cleom.</title> l.c., <foreign lang="greek">φιλιτίων</foreign> all codd. in <title>Phoc.</title> l.c., <foreign lang="greek">φιλίτια</foreign> all codd. in 2.714b, <foreign lang="greek">φιλέστιον</foreign> in 2.697e), <author>Hsch.</author>; <foreign lang="greek">φειδίτια</foreign> in <author>Paus.</author>, <author>Ath.</author> (who cites <author>Antiph.</author>, <author>Dicaearch.Hist.</author>, <author>Phylarch.</author>), <author>Eust.</author>; <foreign lang="greek">φιλίτια</foreign> in <author>X.</author> (v.l. φιδίτια in <title>HG</title> l.c.), <author>Arist.</author> <title>Rh.</title> (<foreign lang="greek">φιδίτια</foreign> Sch.), <author>D.H.</author>, <author>D.Chr.</author>, <author>Philostr.</author>, <author>Them.</author>, <author>Suid.</author>; <i>philitiis</i> in <author>Cic.</author>) </sense>
